And enjoy learning about git and github. :)\n\nScenario for using git, Github and the Github app\n\nBrenda has a party shopping list which she creates as two simple text files (drinks.txt and food.txt) on her computer. She doesn’t want to lose it if her laptop breaks/gets lost. She wants to be able to see the complete history of her changes to the files over time. She also wants to allow other people to see her party shopping list as it might be useful to them. git and github provide the perfect solution.\n\nBrenda sets up her repository on her computer and on github:\n\n\u0010\u0012\u001cSet up a repository\n\nShe puts drinks.txt and food.txt into a folder called party-shopping-list on her computer\nShe drags that folder to her github app and creates a new repository (this now exists only on her computer)\nShe clicks on ‘changes’ to see her current changes (the two files drinks.txt and food.txt have been added)\nShe creates a ‘commit’ (by writing a summary and clicking ‘commit to master’) to save her changes in git history in case she wants to come back to this revision of the files in the future\nShe publishes her repository to github (clicks ‘publish’) so that her commits are now stored on github so her changes are safe and other people can see her party shopping list\n\n\u0011\nHer housemate, Barry, wants to make changes to the party shopping list. Barry also has a github account already.\nBrenda allows Barry to make changes:\n\n\u0010\u0012\u001cAdd a collaborator\n\nShe goes to her github app\nClicks on the party shopping list repository on the left\nClicks on the settings icon\nClicks on ‘View on Github’ - she can now see the repository on the github website\nShe clicks on ‘settings’, then ‘collaborators’ and adds Barry as a collaborator\n\n\u0011\nBarry now wants to edit the party shopping list on his computer:\n\n\u0010\u0012\u001cClone a repository from github to your computer\n\nBarry opens the github app on his computer\nHe clicks the ‘+’ icon in the top left, then ‘clone’, finds the party shopping list repository and the clones it to a folder on his computer\nHe can now see the history of the party shopping list\nHe updates the party shopping list by opening the files (e.g. using sublime) and adding a couple of items to the food and drink lists before saving the files\nHe goes back to the github app and can see his changes in the ‘changes’ tab\nHe creates a ‘commit’ (by writing a summary and clicking ‘commit to master’)\nHe then clicks ‘sync’ to update github with his changes\n\n\u0011\nAnytime Barry or Brenda now want to make changes they need to do the following:\n\n\u0010\u0012\u001cMake changes and share them\nSync - to download any changes from github (from other collaborators)\nEdit - make changes in their favourite text editor (e.g. Sublime)\nCommit - save their set of changes on their own computer\nSync - upload the changes back to github so others can see them\n\n\u0011\n\nDealing with merge conflicts:\nStep 4 above may not work if Brenda and Barry have both made changes to the same file or files at the same time.
